# Analysis of Ground Truth

The GT is:
$$f(A) = -0.2597\sqrt{A} + 0.9123\cos(\log(A + 1))$$

This contains two basis functions:
1. $\sqrt{A}$ â€” an algebraic function
2. $\cos(\log(A+1))$ â€” a transcendental function (composition of cosine and logarithm)

The key question is: can any candidate produce both $\sqrt{A}$ and $\cos(\log(A+1))$ terms?

## Key Observations

The GT contains $\cos(\log(A+1))$, which is a very specific transcendental function. For a candidate to match, it must be able to produce this function or an equivalent form.

Let me categorize the candidates:

### Candidates that are purely rational functions of $A$, $\sqrt{A}$, $A^{3/2}$:
Candidates 1-5, 8-9, 14, 16, 19, 25-26, 29-30, 34-35, 38-49, 51 â€” These are all rational functions of powers of $A$. They cannot produce $\cos(\log(A+1))$. **No match.**

### Candidates with $\exp(A \cdot c)$ terms:
Candidates 6, 7, 15, 17, 20, 21, 22, 31, 37, 55 â€” These contain exponentials $e^{cA}$, which are linearly independent from $\cos(\log(A+1))$. Even combined with rational/polynomial terms, they cannot produce $\cos(\log(A+1))$. **No match.**

### Candidates with $\log(A \cdot c + 1)$ terms:
Candidates 10, 23, 32, 33, 36, 50, 52, 54 â€” These contain $\log(Ac+1)$, which is linearly independent from $\cos(\log(A+1))$. **No match.**

### Candidates with $\sin$ terms:
- **Candidate 18**: $c_0 + c_1\sin(Ac_2+c_3) + c_4\sin(Ac_5+c_6) + c_7\sin(Ac_8+c_9)$ â€” Sum of sinusoids of $A$. These are $\sin(\text{linear in } A)$, not $\cos(\log(A+1))$. **No match.**

- **Candidate 24**: $A^{c_0}c_1 + c_2 + c_3\sin(Ac_4+c_5) + c_6\sin(Ac_7+c_8)$ â€” Has $A^{c_0}$ (can be $\sqrt{A}$) and sinusoids of linear $A$. Cannot produce $\cos(\log(A+1))$. **No match.**

- **Candidate 27, 28**: Rational + $\sin(Ac+c)$. Same issue. **No match.**

- **Candidate 31**: $c_0 e^{Ac_1} + c_2\sin(Ac_3+c_4) + c_5/(Ac_6+c_7)$. **No match.**

- **Candidate 53**: $c_0 + c_1\sin(Ac_2+c_3) + c_4 e^{Ac_5} + c_6\sin(Ac_7+c_8)$. **No match.**

- **Candidate 56**: $\sqrt{A}c_0 + c_1\sin(Ac_2+c_3) + c_4 + c_5\log(Ac_6+1)$. Has $\sqrt{A}$ and $\sin(\text{linear})$ and $\log$. Cannot produce $\cos(\log(A+1))$. **No match.**

- **Candidate 57**: $A^{c_0}c_1 + c_2\sin(Ac_3+c_4) + c_5 + c_6\log(Ac_7+1)$. Same issue. **No match.**

- **Candidate 58**: Rational + $\sin(Ac+c)$ + $1/\sqrt{A}$. **No match.**

### Candidates with $t$ dependence:
Candidates 6, 12, 13, 16, 19, 23, 40 â€” GT has no $t$ dependence. Setting $t$ coefficients to 0 reduces these to other forms already analyzed. **No match.**

### Candidates with both $\exp$ and $\log$:
- **Candidate 13**: Has $\log(Ac+1)$ and $\exp(Ac)$ and $t$. Even zeroing $t$, cannot produce $\cos(\log(A+1))$. **No match.**

- **Candidate 33**: $A^{c_0}c_1 + c_2 + c_3 e^{Ac_4} + c_5\log(Ac_6+1)$. **No match.**

## Conclusion

None of the candidates contain $\cos(\log(\cdot))$ or any combination of functions that could produce it. The function $\cos(\log(A+1))$ is a unique transcendental function that cannot be represented by polynomials, rational functions, exponentials, simple logarithms, or sinusoids of linear arguments.

[NO MATCH]

I need to analyze whether any candidate can exactly match the ground truth:

**GT: `-0.2597*sqrt(A) + 0.9123*cos(log(A + 1))`**

This has two basis functions: `sqrt(A)` and `cos(log(A+1))`.

The key question is: can any candidate's functional form produce `cos(log(A+1))`?

Let me categorize the candidates:

**Candidates that are purely rational functions of A (with powers like A^(3/2), sqrt(A), A, etc.):**
Candidates 1-5, 8-9, 14, 16, 19, 25-26, 29-30, 34-35, 38-48, 51

These are all rational functions of A (ratios of polynomials in sqrt(A)). Rational functions cannot produce `cos(log(A+1))`, which is a transcendental oscillatory function. These are all **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with exponential terms (exp):**
Candidates 6, 7, 15, 17, 20, 21, 22, 31, 32, 33, 36, 37, 50, 53, 55

Exponentials `exp(A*c)` cannot produce `cos(log(A+1))`. The function `cos(log(A+1))` oscillates (albeit with decreasing frequency), while exponentials are monotonic. These are **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with log terms:**
Candidates 10, 11, 23, 52, 54

`log(A+1)` alone (or combined with rational/polynomial terms) cannot produce `cos(log(A+1))`. These are **NO MATCH**.

**Candidates with `t` dependence:**
Candidates 6, 12, 13, 16, 19, 23, 40 - can set `t` coefficients to 0, but still need to check remaining terms. Already covered above.

**Candidates with sin terms:**
- **Candidate 18:** `c0 + c1*sin(A*c2+c3) + c4*sin(A*c5+c6) + c7*sin(A*c8+c9)` â€” sum of sinusoids of `A`. `sin(A*c)` â‰  `cos(log(A+1))`. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 24:** `A^c0*c1 + c2 + c3*sin(A*c4+c5) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8)` â€” same issue. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 27, 28:** Rational + `sin(A*c6+c7)`. `sin(A*c)` â‰  `cos(log(A+1))`. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 31:** `c0*exp(A*c1) + c2*sin(A*c3+c4) + c5/(A*c6+c7)`. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 53:** `c0 + c1*sin(A*c2+c3) + c4*exp(A*c5) + c6*sin(A*c7+c8)`. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 56:** `sqrt(A)*c0 + c1*sin(A*c2+c3) + c4 + c5*log(A*c6+1)`. Has `sqrt(A)` but `sin(A*c2+c3)` â‰  `cos(log(A+1))`. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 57:** `A^c0*c1 + c2*sin(A*c3+c4) + c5 + c6*log(A*c7+1)`. **NO MATCH**.

- **Candidate 58:** Rational + `sin(A*c5+c6)` + `1/sqrt(A)`. **NO MATCH**.

**Candidate 49:** Has `A^(3/2)` and `sqrt(A)` as standalone terms plus rational terms. Still purely algebraic. **NO MATCH**.

None of the candidates contain `cos(log(...))` or any composition that could produce it. The GT requires `cos(log(A+1))`, which is a fundamentally different basis function from anything available in any candidate.
